<script type="text/javascript" language="JavaScript" src="/js/countdown.min.js"></script>

<script>
	
	function clearOtherAmount() {
		$( 'otheramount' ).set( 'value', '' );
	}

	function payCreditCard() {
		var amount = getAmount();
		amount = parseInt( amount, 10 ) * 100;
		var domain = "boardgamegeek.com";
		
		window.location = "https://" + domain + '/support?supporttype=creditcard&amount=' + amount;
	}

	function setPayCreditVisiblity() {

		var aio = $( 'input_amount_other' );
		var fm = $( 'frequency_monthly' );

		if ( aio.checked || fm.checked ) {
			$( 'pay_credit_button' ).set( 'disabled', true );
		}
		else {
			$( 'pay_credit_button' ).set( 'disabled', false );
		}
	}

	function setMonthly() {
		var form = $( 'support-drive-form' );
		form.getElement( 'input[name=cmd]' ).set( 'value', '_xclick-subscriptions' );
		var username = form.getElement( 'input[name=custom]' ).get( 'value' );
		form.getElement( 'input[name=item_name]' ).set( 'value', 'Geek Monthly Support from ' + username );

		addInput( form, 't3', 'M' );
		addInput( form, 'bn', 'PP-SubscriptionsBF' );
		addInput( form, 'p3', '1' );
		addInput( form, 'src', '1' );
		addInput( form, 'sra', '1' );
		addInput( form, 'a3', form.getElement( 'input[name=amount]' ).get( 'value' ) );
	}

	function addInput( form, name, value ) {
		if ( form.getElement( 'input[name=' + name + ']' ) ) {
			form.getElement( 'input[name=' + name + ']' ).set( 'value', value );
		}
		else {
			inputEl = new Element( 'input', {'name': name, 'value': value, 'type': 'hidden'} );
			inputEl.inject( form, 'top' );
		}
	}

	function setOneTime() {
		var form = $( 'support-drive-form' );
		form.getElement( 'input[name=cmd]' ).set( 'value', '_xclick' );
		var username = form.getElement( 'input[name=custom]' ).get( 'value' );
		form.getElement( 'input[name=item_name]' ).set( 'value', 'Geek Support from ' + username );
		destroyInput( form, 't3' );
		destroyInput( form, 'bn' );
		destroyInput( form, 'p3' );
		destroyInput( form, 'src' );
		destroyInput( form, 'sra' );
		destroyInput( form, 'a3' );
	}

	function destroyInput( form, name ) {
		el = form.getElement( 'input[name=' + name + ']' );
		if ( el )
			el.destroy();
	}

	function setAmount( form ) {
		var amount = getAmount();
		form.getElement( 'input[name=amount]' ).set( 'value', amount );
	}

	function getAmount() {
		var supportdiv = $( 'support-amounts' );
		var amount = supportdiv.getElement( 'input[name=amountGiven]' ).get( 'value' );
		if ( !amount ) {
			var amountEls = supportdiv.getElements( 'input[name=amount]' );
			for ( var i = amountEls.length - 1; i >= 0; i-- ) {
				if ( amountEls[ i ].checked ) {
					amount = amountEls[ i ].get( 'value' );
				}
			}
			;
		}

		return amount;
	}

	function submitPayment() {
		var form = $( 'support-drive-form' );

		if ( form.getElement( 'input[name=custom]' ).get( 'value' ) == 'Anonymous User' )
			StickyWin.confirm( "Support", "You are not logged in. If you want to receive a supporter badge and/or adblock (depending on your support level), you should <a href='/login'>log in</a> first! Otherwise, click Ok to continue.", submitPaymentConfirm );
		else
			submitPaymentConfirm();
	}

	function submitPaymentConfirm() {
		var form = $( 'support-drive-form' );

		setAmount( form );
		if ( $( 'frequency_monthly' ).checked ) {
			setMonthly();
		}
		else {
			setOneTime();
		}

		$( 'support-drive-form' ).submit();
	}

	function DismissAppeal() {
		var app = $( 'appeal' );
		app.fade( 'out' ).get( 'tween' ).chain( function () {
			hideAppeal();
		} );
		var myCookie = Cookie.write( 'dismissappeal_v12', 1, {
			duration: 3,
			path: '/',
			domain: '.boardgamegeek.com'
		} );
	}

	function OpenAppeal() {
		showAppeal();
		var oldcookie = Cookie.dispose( 'dismissappeal_v12', {
			path: '/',
			domain: '.boardgamegeek.com'
		});
	}

	function showAppeal() {
		$( 'appeal' ).setStyle( 'display', 'block' );
		$( 'appeal-min' ).setStyle( 'display', 'none' );
		var myFx = new Fx.Tween( $( 'appeal' ), {duration: 2000} );
		myFx.start( 'opacity', 0, 1.0 );
	}

	function hideAppeal() {
		$( 'appeal' ).setStyle( 'display', 'none' );
		$( 'appeal-min' ).setStyle( 'display', 'block' );
	}

	function updateplea() {
		var myCookie = Cookie.read( 'dismissappeal_v12' );

		if ( !myCookie ) {
			showAppeal();
		} else {
			hideAppeal();
		}
	}

	function initSupport() {
		updateplea();
		initTimer();
		addSupportClickEvents();
		resetActiveAmountStyles();
	}

	function initTimer() {
		var enddate = new Date( '2018-01-01T06:00:00.000Z' );
		var now = new Date();
		if ( enddate < now ) {
			$( 'supportcountdown' ).set( 'html', "Now!" );
		}
		else {
			var timerid = countdown( function ( ts ) {
					$( 'supportcountdown' ).set( 'html', ts.toHTML( "span" ) );
				},
				enddate,
				countdown.DAYS | countdown.HOURS | countdown.MINUTES );
		}
	}

	var handleAmountClick = function( event ) {
		var otherClicked = event.target.getParent().getProperty('for') == 'input_amount_other';
		if( !otherClicked )
			clearOtherAmount();
		if( otherClicked ) {
			$( 'input_amount_other' ).set( 'checked', 1 );
		} else {
			event.target.set( 'checked', 1 );
		}
		resetActiveAmountStyles();
		setPayCreditVisiblity();
	};

	var resetActiveAmountStyles = function() {
		$$('fieldset.support-drive-contribute-amounts input[name=amount]' ).each( function( el ){
			if( el.checked )
				el.getParent().addClass( 'active' );
			else
				el.getParent().removeClass( 'active' );
		});
	};

	function addSupportClickEvents() {
		var buttons = $$('fieldset.support-drive-contribute-amounts input' ).each( function( el ){
			el.addEvent( 'click', handleAmountClick );
		});
	};

	//	window.addEvent( 'domready', initSupport );
	initSupport();
	
</script>

			Well, it's that time of the year, again. The people's choice solo list submissions are closed and everyone in the 1PG is excitedly awaiting the notification that a new GeekList has been posted. I love seeing how the solo community collectively ranks each year's hot solo games among the tried-and true games of yesteryear, but half the fun for me is organizing my own list.<br /><br />This is my third year voting in the people's choice list. 2016 was by far my best year for solo gaming. 2017 has been <i>okay</i> for me, but I've had a steep decline in time, energy, and motivation to play board games as of late. Still, solo gaming is my favorite part of this hobby, and I couldn't in good conscience abstain from the vote. While I heavily relied on my top 20 from last year (even without recently playing a good chunk of the games on said list), the order has changed a fair bit and there are also a fair number of new entries. So without further ado....

						<dd class="doubleright">
									#20<br /><br />Funnily enough, this was my #1 game last year. I had learned it fairly recently and was playing often. While I still think highly of the game, I haven't played it since last year. I'd love to set it up again, but that would require a reread of the rules. And I think that's the biggest (and probably most commonly cited) problem with this game: it work so well, it all makes sense, but the intricacies of the ruleset require you to play regularly or forget. I've forgotten, and while I'm sure re-learning would be much simpler that learning the game for the first time, my time has been at a premium lately. I hope to revisit this one soon.

	<a href="/support"  class='js_badgelink'
		onmouseover="GAV_ShowBadge( this ); return overlib( 'This user supports the website - Click for more info.', WRAP );"
		onmouseout="return nd();">
	<span class='oddicon patron'></span><span class='oddicon year_14_band band' data-year='14'></span><span class='oddicon year_15_num num last' data-year='15'></span>	</a>
</div>
		
	<div ><a href="/microbadge/1506"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1506_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1507"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1507_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1601"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1601_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1508"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1508_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1602"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1602_0.gif"></a></div>
</div>
</dd>
						<dd class="doubleright">
									#19<br /><br />The first of many worker placement games on my list. I own and play a lot of euro games, but this one holds a unique spot in my collection. It doesn't feel anything like a Rosenberg game, and it has a lot of variability, especially considering the relatively low number of action spaces and lack of automated opponent. The weight and length of this game make it a pleasant experience for nearly any occasion. 
								<div class='clear'></div>
			</dd>
		</dl>

</dd>
						<dd class="doubleright">
									#18<br /><br />Before receiving and playing this game, I expected it to rank much higher on the list. After playing a handful of times, I wasn't sure it'd even make the list. But when I started looking at my most-played games from the past year, this one was pretty close to the top. <br /><br />One of the best things about this game is that if you want a longer, more involved game, you can play that way. If you want a quick game, you can do that, too. I do feel like you have to play at least two, ideally three eras to get the most out of it. I'm not crazy about the spatial movement aspect of the game, but it does keep things fresh. 
								<div class='clear'></div>
			</dd>

						<dd class="doubleright">
									#17<br /><br />This was another very high-ranked game on my previous list. I still think it's a great game, but over time, I've come to value elegant games even more. As far as huge euro games go, the rules overhead for this one isn't too bad. And while I like the way the solo game gives you the ability to explore a variety of different options, I really appreciate Rosenberg's tighter games. I think this one is good and will likely always have it in my collection, but I'm often more likely to reach for some of his older titles.

						<dd class="doubleright">
									#15<br /><br />It was tough trying to narrow down which Viard game(s) to put on the list. I couldn't justify putting this one, Card City, and Small City on the list--while all are great in different ways, they have so much in common that were I to cull my collection to 20 games, they wouldn't all make the cut. So in a way, Town Center's inclusion on this list is representative of the trilogy of games. It's also the game I've played the most of the three, and I think it's the most clever of the three, as well. <br /><br />Never has a game with such simple rules burned my brain so much. The 3D aspect really adds a fresh twist to the city-building genre. Is there a more elegant solable game? If so, I haven't played it. 
								<div class='clear'></div>
			</dd>

</dd>
						<dd class="doubleright">
									#14<br /><br />I've only ever played this game solo. It's small, it's quick, it's everything I like about 4x games minus everything I dislike about them. It has just enough euro elements to draw me in, and just enough conflict to keep things interesting. I still haven't played the expansion yet--if it fleshes out the solo experience like I expect it to, I expect this game to rise on next year's list. 
								<div class='clear'></div>

</dd>
						<dd class="doubleright">
									#12<br /><br />I must confess, I still haven't participated in the guild's Rallyman cup. But I've had a blast playing it on my own. I love push-your-luck, and this game does it so well. Even without opponents to compete against, I find racing through a tricky curve to be both exhilarating and rewarding. One of these days, I'll join the fold and try to put my times up on the board. Until then, I'll be having fun doing time trials.
								<div class='clear'></div>

	<a href="/support"  class='js_badgelink'
		onmouseover="GAV_ShowBadge( this ); return overlib( 'This user supports the website - Click for more info.', WRAP );"
		onmouseout="return nd();">
	<span class='oddicon patron'></span><span class='oddicon year_14_band band' data-year='14'></span><span class='oddicon year_15_num num last' data-year='15'></span>	</a>
</div>
		
	<div ><a href="/microbadge/1506"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1506_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1507"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1507_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1601"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1601_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1508"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1508_0.gif"></a><a href="/microbadge/1602"><img alt='mb'  onmouseover="return overlib('Modern Art fan', WRAP );" onmouseout="return nd();" title=''src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw=="onload="lzld(this)"onerror="lzld(this)"class='mbimg'data-frz-src="//cf.geekdo-static.com/mbs/mb_1602_0.gif"></a></div>
</div>
</dd>
						<dd class="doubleright">
									#11<br /><br />When I submitted my list to Kevin, I wrote Limes instead of Cities. I figured that title was a bit more popular and had a better choice of charting on the top 100. But Cities is almost the same game, and I like it slightly more. I keep a set of tiles and meeples in my luggage and try to play this one in every new city I visit. It's my most-played game for 2017, and I'm not tired of it in the least. It's probably the shortest game on my list, but it always keeps me interested. If you're into tile laying games, you owe it to yourself to check this one out. 
								<div class='clear'></div>
			</dd>
		</dl>

						<dd class="doubleright">
									#6<br /><br />This is another Rosenberg title that moved up my list this year. While I initially thought that Odin was a strict improvement, I've since changed my mind. Arle does a lot to reward specialization, and I find that to be a very attractive quality. While there might not be as much variety in this game as there is in Odin, I find it fun to pick a route and stick with it over the course of the game. I'm definitely anticipating Arle's upcoming expansion.

						<dd class="doubleright">
									#5<br /><br />Opinion: The Cure is the greatest cooperative game ever made. It just hits all the right spots for me. It's easy to setup, quick to play, has tons of variety, uses dice in a unique and fun way, contains lots of challenging choices, and most importantly, is just plain fun. The expansion content really elevates the game, and I don't see this one ever leaving my collection.
								<div class='clear'></div>
			</dd>

						<dd class="doubleright">

									#3<br /><br />Out of all of Rosenberg's big box games, this one is probably the most unique. </div>
</dd>
						<dd class="doubleright">
									#2<br /><br />The best euro game ever made? I certainly think so. In fact, while I like The Colonists, playing that one has only made me appreciate Roads & Boats even more. For many players, the lack of in-game randomness kills R&B as a solo game. I personally like trying to improve upon my previous scores, but even aside from that, it's easy to construct new maps and scenarios to play. I love R&B's bulky box, goofy cover art, and even the clunky map overlay and dry-erase marker. It's in a class all of its own and has provided many hours of quiet, calculated fun. Here's to many more. 
								<div class='clear'></div>
			</dd>

						<dd class="doubleright">
									#1<br /><br />Hoplomachus: Origins was actually my intro to the series. I really enjoyed it, but it was just a little too short. Playthroughs ended a little too soon and left me wanting just a little more. Rise of Rome is, in my opinion, a much more satisfying experience. I also like how you're typically fighting (and performing upkeep for) one very strong enemy as opposed to several smaller ones. <br /><br />I have to admit, one part of why I love this game is the stellar components. I've added the premium health chips, leather dice tray, and alloy dice to my collection. It's all so satisfying to handle and manipulate, and while I love the mechanics and gameplay, the components definitely help make this title one of the cornerstones of my collection.<br /><br />It should also be noted that I don't tend to gravitate towards Ameritrash/thematic games. Hoplo is just really unique and I can't get enough of it. It's straightforward, yet full of keyword-induced variety that keeps every game fresh. And the way that dice rolls control the Titan AI keeps things simple and unpredictable as well. <br /><br />I'm proud to call Rise of Rome my favorite game, and I absolutely plan on tracking down any and all future Hoplomachus content. If you haven't played this one, try to get your hands on a copy...I think you'll like it. 
								<div class='clear'></div>
			</dd>

Could you expand on why you like Rise of Rome better a bit more? Does Ithe have a lot of solo replayability? I would like to read you on that &lt;img src=\&quot;https:\/\/cf.geekdo-static.com\/images\/smile.gif\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; border=\&quot;0\&quot; \/&gt;. &lt;\/div&gt;&lt;br \/&gt;&lt;br \/&gt;Origins has its strengths. The units have more varied abilities, the different arenas keep things interesting, and the campaign-like trial system is a plus if you&#039;re into that.&lt;br \/&gt;&lt;br \/&gt;But I see Origins as a snack, and Rise of Rome is more like a Meal. Games are two or three times longer than the trials in Origins, and I find them that much more exciting. The Titans are big and bad. They also all have their own schtick that&#039;s, in my opinion, more unique and exciting than the boss abilities in Origins. &lt;br \/&gt;&lt;br \/&gt;Aside from the Titans, there are some neat ideas in RoR that didn&#039;t carry over to Origins. For example, dealing damage to the Titans you fight gains you crowd favor points, which can be used to unlock additional units and abilities. You have to balance you strategy around ramping up your crowd favor and unlocking new abilities really facing the Titan head on. Plus, the map is sizably bigger, which presents more opportunities for tactical maneuvering and evading.&lt;br \/&gt;&lt;br \/&gt;For me personally, less upkeep is always better. Rise of Rome, despite being bigger, is also a bit simpler than Origins. Instead of consulting charts and dice rolls for multiple enemy units, you roll the dice once and generally only have to carry out actions for one enemy. I love how easy the game is to manage. &lt;br \/&gt;&lt;br \/&gt;If you&#039;re looking for a reason to add more Hoplo to your collection, remember that your Origins units will enhance the armies in RoR and the new chips in RoR will enhance your drafting options in Origins. If I could only have one, I think I&#039;d go with Rise of Rome, but they definitely complement each other well. &quot;,&quot;avatar&quot;:&quot;&lt;div class=&#039;avatarblock js-avatar &#039; data-userid=&#039;807976&#039;
